24:601:51211:18:0:72:218:71:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:college or more in some models. 
25:602:51291:0:28:72:527:704:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:attend centers that do not participate in CACFP drink two or more cups of milk per day versus 
25:603:51385:28:27:72:523:676:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:nearly 71% of those at participating centers.  For fruits and vegetables, the increases are from 
25:604:51482:27:28:72:310:649:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:38% to 43% and from 33% to 42%, respectively. 
25:605:51528:28:28:108:540:621:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:In contrast, we find limited evidence that CACFP is associated with weight status or food 
25:606:51618:28:27:72:532:593:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:insecurity (see again Table 7).  There is some evidence that children at participating centers are 
25:607:51717:27:28:72:541:566:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:more likely to be healthy weight than underweight; predicted probabilities indicate that about 8% 
25:608:51815:28:27:72:529:538:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:are underweight at non-participating centers versus about 3% at participating centers, based on 
25:609:51911:27:28:72:509:511:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Column 4.  Regarding overweight, about one-third of all poor four-year olds in centers are 
25:610:52002:28:28:72:506:483:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:overweight (not shown in tables), and being healthy versus overweight is not significantly 
25:611:52093:28:27:72:525:455:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:associated with CACFP participation (Table 7).  Regarding food insecurity, on average, about 
25:612:52186:27:28:72:503:428:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:40% of all poor children who are in centers at four years have some household-level food 
25:613:52275:28:27:72:532:400:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:insecurity and about 25% of these children are themselves food insecure (not shown in tables).  
25:614:52371:27:28:72:526:373:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:The coefficient for CACFP-participation in Table 7 is small, never statistically significant and 
25:615:52468:28:28:72:526:345:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:usually (unexpectedly) positive in sign for household and child food insecurity.  However, the 
25:616:52563:28:27:72:538:317:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:coefficient for child food insecurity reverses in sign to the expected negative direction in models 
25:617:52663:27:28:72:539:290:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:with lagged outcomes (Column 4 of Table 7).  Indeed, we saw in Table 6 that children who were 
25:618:52757:28:27:72:525:262:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:food insecure at age two were more likely to attend a CACFP-participating center at age four. 
25:619:52851:27:28:108:541:235:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Appendix E presents sensitivity analyses, re-estimating the models with minimal controls 
25:620:52940:28:28:72:520:207:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:for children who were not in care at two years of age, who were in care 30 or more hours per 
25:621:53033:28:27:72:508:179:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:week, and for children who were in community centers (as opposed to pre-kindergarten or 
25:622:53121:27:28:72:541:152:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:preschool).  The associations between CACFP participation and milk and vegetable consumption 
25:623:53214:28:27:72:541:124:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:remained significantly positive and of similar magnitude in the models restricted to children who 
25:624:53312:27:28:72:495:97:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:had not been in care at two years (Appendix E, Column 3).  The coefficients of CACFP 
25:625:53397:28:0:72:532:69:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:participation for children who are in care longer hours or in community centers are consistently 
26:626:53542:0:28:72:539:704:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:positive and sometimes larger than for the full sample, but significant only for milk consumption 
26:627:53640:28:27:72:513:676:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(Appendix E, Columns 1 and 2).  Although we had expected the coefficients might be even 
26:628:53728:27:28:72:542:649:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:larger for children with greater exposure to the care setting, it is also possible that children whose 
26:629:53831:28:28:72:533:621:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:parents put them in longer hours of care and in community settings may be selectively different 
26:630:53927:28:27:72:366:593:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:than children placed in care for fewer hours or in preschool.  
26:631:53990:27:28:108:526:566:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:In summary, among lower-income children, attending a CACFP-participating center is 
26:632:54073:28:27:72:540:538:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:associated with greater consumption of milk, vegetables, and (to some extent) fruits at four years 
26:633:54172:27:28:72:506:511:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of age.  In addition, poor children at CACFP participating centers are no more likely to be 
26:634:54264:28:28:72:541:483:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:overweight and are less likely to be underweight than children at non-participating centers.  Food 
26:635:54363:28:27:72:500:455:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:insecurity does not differ between poor children attending CACFP-participating and non-
26:636:54450:27:28:72:176:428:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:participating centers. 
26:637:54473:28:27:108:111:400:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A: 
26:638:54473:27:28:72:205:373:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:C:Summary and Discussion 
26:639:54496:28:28:108:538:345:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:To our knowledge, this is the first study to provide a national portrait of the determinants 
26:640:54589:28:27:72:502:317:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of receiving CACFP benefits and the association of CACFP participation with children’s 
26:641:54676:27:28:72:509:290:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:nutrition-related outcomes.  Our results reveal that the CACFP program misses many poor 
26:642:54764:28:27:72:542:262:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:children, and a sizable fraction of non-poor children participate in the program. Coverage of poor 
26:643:54863:27:28:72:523:235:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:children is particularly limited at age two because over 80% of two-year olds are cared for by 
26:644:54958:28:28:72:538:207:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:parents at home or in an unlicensed child care home, and family poverty rates are relatively high 
26:645:55056:28:27:72:514:179:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:for two-year old children who are cared for in these settings.  The program reaches a higher 
26:646:55149:27:28:72:520:152:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:fraction of poor four-year olds because many poor children spend time in Head Start centers, 
26:647:55242:28:27:72:527:124:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:where CACFP participation rates are nearly 100%, or in other participating centers.  Yet, poor 
26:648:55337:27:28:72:526:97:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:children who are cared for in centers are much less likely to receive CACFP when they live in 
26:649:55431:28:0:72:533:69:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:wealthier areas than when they live in poorer areas, especially if they attend a for-profit center.  
27:650:55580:0:28:72:540:704:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Furthermore, even at four years, nearly 40% of children are cared for by parents at home or in an 
27:651:55678:28:27:72:516:676:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:unlicensed child care home, and a relatively high proportion of children in these settings are 
27:652:55773:27:28:72:535:649:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:poor.  Licensed family day care is notable because few children are cared for in these settings at 
27:653:55872:28:28:72:516:621:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:either two years or four years, and there is little variation in CACFP participation by family, 
27:654:55968:28:27:72:200:593:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:provider, or area poverty.  
27:655:55996:27:28:108:537:566:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:We also found that provider, family, and locational characteristics all affect participation 
27:656:56089:28:27:72:491:538:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in CACFP.  As noted, poor children who reside in low-income areas are more likely to 
27:657:56174:27:28:72:512:511:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:participate in CACFP than poor children in wealthier areas.  CACFP participation is higher 
27:658:56265:28:28:72:509:483:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:among parents of lower socioeconomic status and whose children are in care more hours.   
27:659:56354:28:27:72:518:455:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Provider characteristics clearly matter. Large, licensed, accredited and non-profit centers are 
27:660:56450:27:28:72:528:428:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:more likely to participate, as are those connected to Head Start through referrals (or who serve 
27:661:56547:28:27:72:507:400:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:children who are also served by Head Start).  These results are broadly consistent with the 
27:662:56639:27:28:72:523:373:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:conclusion reached by Currie (2006b) that standard transaction costs (and benefits) as well as 
27:663:56734:28:28:72:512:345:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:administrative burden importantly affect the take-up of social programs (though our results 
27:664:56826:28:27:72:327:317:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:would also suggest a role for information networks). 
27:665:56879:27:28:108:539:290:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, we found evidence that CACFP is associated with increased milk, vegetable, and 
27:666:56967:28:27:72:519:262:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(to some extent) fruit consumption and lower prevalence of underweight among low-income 
27:667:57055:27:28:72:510:235:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:four-year olds in centers.  The associations with milk, vegetables, and healthy weight were 
27:668:57147:28:28:72:499:207:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:robust to inclusion of detailed child, family and provider controls, including lagged milk 
27:669:57238:28:27:72:533:179:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:consumption and lagged food insecurity. The findings for milk persisted when we restricted the 
27:670:57333:27:28:72:528:152:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sample to children in care full-time and to those not in care at age two.  We found no evidence 
27:671:57429:28:27:72:535:124:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:that CACFP increased the prevalence of overweight among this group of four-year olds, and we 
27:672:57522:27:28:71:536:97:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:also found no evidence for an association with child or household food insecurity. Evidence that 
27:673:57619:28:0:71:540:69:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the program may benefit participating children underscores the importance of the finding that the 
28:674:57765:0:28:72:364:704:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:program fails to reach a substantial portion of poor children. 
28:675:57828:28:27:108:534:676:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:It is worth considering what the rationale might be for a nutrition redistribution program 
28:676:57919:27:28:72:528:649:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:that does not reach all poor children, and that treats poor children differently depending on the 
28:677:58017:28:28:72:508:621:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:characteristics of their child care provider.  Considering how CACFP intersects with other 
28:678:58108:28:27:72:499:593:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:nutritional and child care subsidy program is revealing in this regard.  Consider first that 
28:679:58201:27:28:72:502:566:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:consuming food away from home in child care (including when meals are paid for by the 
28:680:58287:28:27:72:523:538:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:CACFP program) does not reduce eligibility for, or benefits from, other nutritional assistance 
28:681:58382:27:28:72:521:511:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:programs (such as Food Stamps/SNAP or WIC).  Whether this rule advances redistributional 
28:682:58471:28:28:72:526:483:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:objectives depends in part on the goals of the CACFP program, the economic incidence of the 
28:683:58563:28:27:72:536:455:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:subsidy, and the impact of the different food subsidy programs on food consumption. If CACFP 
28:684:58656:27:28:72:534:428:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:is meant to subsidize meals consumed away from home by poor children, and Food Stamps and 
28:685:58746:28:27:72:514:400:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:WIC benefit amounts are set optimally, then Food Stamp or WIC benefits would have to be 
28:686:58834:27:28:72:504:373:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:adjusted downward if CACFP raises children’s food consumption.9  On the other hand, if 
28:687:58921:28:28:71:535:345:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:CACFP is meant to augment inadequate levels of Food Stamps and WIC benefits, then it would 
28:688:59012:28:27:71:533:317:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:be more efficient to raise the benefit amounts in those programs to an adequate level, or, failing 
28:689:59111:27:28:71:534:290:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:that, to make all low-income children eligible for CACFP, regardless of provider characteristics 
28:690:59208:28:27:71:517:262:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(including poor children cared for in their own homes).  A third possibility is that CACFP is 
28:691:59302:27:28:71:536:235:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:conditioned on care outside the home because it is intended to reward employment by offsetting 
28:692:59397:28:28:71:532:207:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:costs to families associated with holding a job, the most important of which are child care costs 
28:693:59495:28:7:71:219:179:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:                                                 
28:694:59543:7:18:72:527:172:49:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:9 Anecdotal evidence suggests that most providers supply meals, rather than having parents send meals 
28:695:59645:18:13:72:530:154:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:with children, and our data shows that 95 percent or more of providers report serving meals and snacks. 
28:696:59749:13:12:72:520:141:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:Thus, Food Stamps and WIC benefits must cover fewer of the families’ total food consumption when 
28:697:59846:12:13:72:532:129:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:children are in child care.  Providers might include meal costs in fees. But, families will not directly pay 
28:698:59955:13:13:72:523:116:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:these fees if their care is covered by CCDF child care subsidies, thus they are effectively better off (in 
28:699:60062:13:12:72:526:103:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:terms of total food subsidies) than comparable families whose children are not in care.  And, if they do 
28:700:60167:12:13:72:526:91:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:pay the fees directly, including the child’s meal costs, then they are left with less fungible income than 
28:701:60274:13:13:72:535:78:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:they would be if more food subsidies went directly to the provider (since Food Stamps and WIC must be 
28:702:60376:13:0:72:310:65:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:spent on foods, and a limited bundle of foods at that). 
29:703:60480:0:28:72:535:704:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and the implicit tax on earnings inherent in means-testing benefits.  Nonetheless, if other means-
29:704:60578:28:27:72:522:676:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:tested nutritional assistance benefits are set optimally, it would be more efficient to use direct 
29:705:60677:27:28:71:529:649:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(cash) subsidies to child care to promote employment of the poor, rather than link eligibility to 
29:706:60775:28:28:72:452:621:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:provider characteristics or characteristics of other children in the care setting.   
29:707:60860:28:27:108:526:593:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:It is also worth considering the rationale for more stringent eligibility requirements for 
29:708:60951:27:28:72:526:566:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:for-profit than non-profit centers. One possibility is that these different payment schedules are 
29:709:61049:28:27:72:541:538:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:intended as a crude quality-adjustment of the subsidy (see, e.g., Blau 2001) under the assumption 
29:710:61147:27:28:72:527:511:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:that non-profit centers are of higher quality, on average, than for-profit centers (Cleveland and 
29:711:61245:28:28:72:525:483:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Krashinsky 2009).  Policymakers might similarly have made eligibility criteria more stringent 
29:712:61339:28:27:72:534:455:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:among for-profit centers out of concern that for-profit centers are more likely to use the subsidy 
29:713:61438:27:28:72:518:428:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:to increase profit rather than to increase the quality of care.  However, even if quality of non-
29:714:61535:28:27:72:531:400:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:profit centers is higher, on average, because there is substantial variation in quality within each 
29:715:61635:27:28:72:528:373:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sector, it would be more efficient to target quality directly with quality-adjusted subsidies than 
29:716:61734:28:28:72:533:345:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:with a nutritional subsidy that is higher for care in the non-profit sector.  States are increasingly 
29:717:61836:28:27:72:507:317:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:adopting Quality Rating and Improvement Systems to provide such tiered reimbursement, 
29:718:61922:27:28:72:510:290:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:although they have not been rigorously evaluated (National Child Care Information Center 
29:719:62011:28:27:72:106:262:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:2009). 
29:720:62018:27:28:108:513:235:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Policymakers may similarly have excluded license-exempt homes from the national 
29:721:62098:28:28:72:532:207:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:CACFP rules to assure some oversight or to assure of a lower bound on quality for settings that 
29:722:62194:28:27:72:538:179:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:receive public subsidy. This practice would be in contrast to federal policy in the Child Care and 
29:723:62293:27:28:72:510:152:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Development Fund (CCDF) which provides general child care subsidies.  In the 1980s and 
29:724:62380:28:27:72:541:124:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:1990s, the CCDF program moved increasingly toward reimbursing whatever type of care parents 
29:725:62472:27:28:72:530:97:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:choose, including license-exempt care (Kahn and Kamerman 1987; U.S. Department of Health 
29:726:62561:28:0:72:542:69:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and Human Services 2009).  Nationally, one-quarter of children who receive CCDF subsidies are 
30:727:62703:0:28:72:530:704:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in license-exempt care; in some states as many as two-thirds are in such care (U.S. Department 
30:728:62798:28:27:72:533:676:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of Health and Human Services 2008).  This inclusion of settings outside of the licensing system 
30:729:62894:27:28:72:508:649:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:may reflect a combination of a preference for supporting parental choice, a need to rapidly 
30:730:62986:28:28:72:508:621:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:increase the supply of care when the welfare reforms of the 1990s required parents to seek 
30:731:63077:28:27:72:521:593:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:employment, and evidence that small home-based and unregulated settings are not inferior to 
30:732:63169:27:28:72:507:566:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:licensed settings, at least according to some definitions of quality (such as the warmth and 
30:733:63262:28:27:72:531:538:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sensitivity of caregivers to infants and toddlers, NICHD 1996; and flexibility to parental needs, 
30:734:63360:27:28:72:519:511:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:but not developmental quality, Li-Grining, and Coley 2006).  Whatever the impetus, the two 
30:735:63451:28:28:72:523:483:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:subsidies (food subsidy and general subsidy) for child care differ in this respect.  It is also the 
30:736:63551:28:27:72:507:455:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:case that if the general child care subsidy were set optimally, an additional child care food 
30:737:63645:27:28:72:522:428:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:subsidy would be inefficient.10 If the general subsidy is too low, it would be more efficient to 
30:738:63742:28:27:72:521:400:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:increase it than to have a separate food subsidy (unless perhaps the food subsidy’s nutritional 
30:739:63838:27:28:72:535:373:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:training and menu requirements are effective in increasing the nutritional quality of food, which 
30:740:63936:28:28:72:239:345:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:our results suggest they may be).   
30:741:63972:28:27:108:542:317:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:State child care regulations often include nutritional standards that states use to attempt to 
30:742:64067:27:28:72:518:290:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:improve nutrition in licensed settings.  In a review of state regulations Sara E. Benjamin and 
30:743:64162:28:27:72:514:262:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:colleagues (2009) found that 10 states’ regulations for centers and 27 states’ regulations for 
30:744:64257:27:28:72:492:235:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:homes included none of the standards recommended by the National Health and Safety 
30:745:64340:28:28:72:492:207:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Performance Standards.  A related review found that fewer than 10 states limited sugar 
30:746:64427:28:27:72:499:179:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sweetened beverages and foods of low nutritional value in child care licensing standards 
30:747:64516:27:28:72:189:152:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(Benjamin et al. 2008).  
30:748:64541:28:8:72:219:124:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:                                                 
30:749:64589:8:17:72:519:116:49:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:10 CCDF reimbursement rates are set by states.  Federal guidelines require states to regularly conduct 
30:750:64692:17:13:71:542:99:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:market rate surveys and recommend that reimbursement rates be 75th percentile of market rates.  The most 
30:751:64797:13:13:71:522:86:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:recent state plans indicate that half the states set their reimbursement rates below this benchmark, and 
30:752:64902:13:0:71:527:73:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:rates range from the 10th to the 85th percentile (U.S. Department of Health and Human Services 2009).  
31:753:65053:0:28:108:538:704:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:In sum, the CACFP eligibility and benefit rules result in some undesirable efficiency and 
31:754:65143:28:27:71:519:676:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:equity properties because equity criteria (especially poverty reduction) would require greater 
31:755:65238:27:28:71:526:649:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:targeting of poor children and less reliance on provider characteristics, and because efficiency 
31:756:65335:28:28:71:530:621:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:would be enhanced either by using direct, cash child care subsidies (possibly quality-adjusted), 
31:757:65432:28:27:71:515:593:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:by increasing nutritional assistance through the Food Stamps or WIC programs, or by states 
31:758:65523:27:28:71:530:566:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:increasing the nutritional requirements in child care licensing standards.  Still, political support 
31:759:65624:28:27:71:534:538:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:may be greater for a nutritional subsidy than a cash subsidy, or for a subsidy to child care rather 
31:760:65724:27:28:71:445:511:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:than one that would also benefit poor families that care for children at home.  
31:761:65804:28:28:107:516:483:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:We are left with the conclusion that the structure of the CACFP program most likely 
31:762:65888:28:28:71:328:455:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:reflects a compromise among multiple goals such as: 
31:763:65940:28:29:89:330:427:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f3:A: provide nutritional assistance to poor children 
31:764:65989:29:28:89:351:398:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f3:A: promote employment among low-income families 
31:765:66035:28:28:89:521:370:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f3:A: support care providers who have low incomes or who serve low-income communities 
31:766:66116:28:28:89:355:342:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f3:A: provide greater support to higher quality child care 
31:767:66170:28:28:71:490:314:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Different individuals will attach different weights to each of these goals. More explicit 
31:768:66260:28:27:71:517:286:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:consideration and agreement about any or a subset of these goals might lead to an assistance 
31:769:66353:27:28:71:509:259:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:program that achieved distributional objectives more efficiently. The results for child food 
31:770:66446:28:27:71:542:231:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:consumption and healthy weight that we present provide some evidence that the first (nutritional) 
31:771:66544:27:28:71:530:204:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:goal may be met to some degree (although additional research is needed to replicate this result, 
31:772:66641:28:28:71:521:176:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:ideally with a stronger causal design).  The evidence on program coverage we present should 
31:773:66733:28:27:71:511:148:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:help policymakers and analysts understand who is and is not being served by CACFP, and, 
31:774:66821:27:0:71:507:121:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:therefore, to suggest the trade-offs in attempting to reach the full range of possible goals.

45:1389:104919:0:28:168:482:704:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Appendix A: Measures in the ECLS-B and Descriptive Statistics 
45:1390:104981:28:27:108:514:676:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:A:CACFP participation.—At the two year follow up, center directors and home-based 
45:1391:105061:27:28:72:527:649:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f6:B:providers were asked: Do you receive commodities or cash reimbursement from the Child and 
45:1392:105151:28:28:72:544:621:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:B:Adult Care Food Program or the Child Care Food Program for the meals and snacks you serve?  
45:1393:105243:28:27:72:528:593:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:The question was skipped when care was provided by a relative or when the care took place in 
45:1394:105336:27:28:72:514:566:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f6:B:the child’s home.  At the four year follow up, center directors were asked: Do you currently 
45:1395:105429:28:27:72:529:538:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:C:receive reimbursement from the United States Department of Agriculture (USDA) for meals or 
45:1396:105520:27:28:71:538:511:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:C:snacks served to children in your {center/program}? And home-based providers were asked: Do 
45:1397:105612:28:28:72:527:483:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:C:you participate in the Child and Adult Care Food Program (CACFP), or the Child Care Food 
45:1398:105701:28:27:72:509:455:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:B:Program for the meals and snacks you serve? At the four year follow up, the question was 
45:1399:105789:27:28:72:527:428:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:skipped only for providers of care in the child’s home (relatives in another home answered the 
45:1400:105884:28:27:72:541:400:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:question).  At both waves, we coded the small fraction (5% or less) of centers and homes that did 
45:1401:105982:27:28:72:496:373:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:not serve meals or snacks as non-participants.  At neither wave were participating home 
45:1402:106070:28:28:71:383:345:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f6:B:providers asked if they received Tier I or Tier II reimbursement. 
45:1403:106135:28:27:107:536:317:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:A:CACFP reimbursement levels.—We use information about the family, provider, and ZIP 
45:1404:106218:27:28:71:527:290:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:code poverty to approximate eligibility rules and reimbursement levels.  Of the several criteria 
45:1405:106315:28:27:71:527:262:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:that can be used to demonstrate eligibility for Tier I reimbursement levels (see Figure 1), prior 
45:1406:106413:27:28:71:538:235:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:research has found that nearly three-quarters of Tier I providers are determined eligible based on 
45:1407:106512:28:28:72:538:207:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:local school data (Gordon et al. 2008).  We merged National Center for Education Statistics data 
45:1408:106609:28:27:72:540:179:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:about elementary schools in the family’s ZIP code and classified ZIP codes according to whether 
45:1409:106705:27:28:72:518:152:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in none, some, or all of these schools were at least 50% of pupils eligible for free or reduced-
45:1410:106801:28:27:72:503:124:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:price lunch.  The next most commonly used criterion for Tier I homes is provider income 
45:1411:106889:27:0:72:536:97:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(Gordon et al. 2008).  Although we lacked complete information about the provider’s household 
46:1412:107031:0:28:72:537:704:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:size, we approximated provider eligibility based on whether the provider’s income was above or 
46:1413:107126:28:27:71:538:676:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:below $40,000 (approximately 185% of the poverty threshold for a family of four in 2005).  The 
46:1414:107221:27:28:71:530:649:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:least common criterion to determine homes’ eligibility for Tier I reimbursement is local census 
46:1415:107317:28:28:71:537:621:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:data (Gordon et al. 2008); however, local poverty may better approximate the benefits to centers 
46:1416:107414:28:27:71:531:593:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of participating.  Thus, we also merged data from the U.S. Decennial Census of Population and 
46:1417:107508:27:28:71:537:566:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:classified ZIP codes to determine whether fewer than 10%, 10 to 19%, or 20% or more of young 
46:1418:107601:28:27:71:525:538:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:children (under age 5) in the ZIP code had family incomes below 100% of the federal poverty 
46:1419:107693:27:28:71:524:511:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:level.  The two measures of local area poverty (school lunch program eligibility and ZIP code 
46:1420:107787:28:28:71:339:483:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:poverty rates) are highly correlated (see Appendix B).   
46:1421:107844:28:27:107:512:455:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:The ECLS-B study child’s eligibility for the highest reimbursement levels in Tier II 
46:1422:107929:27:28:71:512:428:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:homes and in centers was based on whether their household income fell below 185% of the 
46:1423:108017:28:27:71:537:400:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:federal poverty line (FPL) for a household of their size (Snow et al. 2007: 405-411) and whether 
46:1424:108114:27:28:71:541:373:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the family participated in TANF or Food Stamps.  When we refer to poor or low-income children 
46:1425:108208:28:28:71:529:345:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:we mean those who meet any of these individual eligibility criteria (less than or equal to 185% 
46:1426:108304:28:27:71:279:317:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:FPL or receiving TANF or Food Stamps).  
46:1427:108344:27:28:107:537:290:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:A:Type of child care provider.—We classified children according to whether the child was: 
46:1428:108432:28:27:71:535:262:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(1) not in care, (2) in unlicensed care, either in their own home or by a relative in another home, 
46:1429:108532:27:28:71:536:235:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(3) in unlicensed care by a non-relative in another home, (4) in licensed family day care, (5) in a 
46:1430:108632:28:28:71:513:207:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:for-profit non-Head Start center (referred to as for-profit center for simplicity), (6) in a non-
46:1431:108729:28:27:71:508:179:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:profit non-Head Start center (referred to as non-profit center), or (7) in a Head Start center 
46:1432:108824:27:28:72:502:152:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(referred to as Head Start).  The parent reported whether or not the child was in care, and 
46:1433:108916:28:27:71:500:124:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:provider interviews determined the type of care.  Children who were in multiple types of 
46:1434:109005:27:0:71:472:97:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:arrangements were classified based on the setting where they spent the most hours. 
47:1435:109136:0:28:72:533:704:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Approximately 19% of children were in more than one care arrangement and, on average, these 
47:1436:109228:28:27:72:381:676:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:children spent 65% of their time in care in their primary setting. 
47:1437:109295:27:28:108:518:649:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:A:Child and family covariates.—Child and family covariates were chosen because they 
47:1438:109377:28:28:72:485:621:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:might predict whether the child attended a participating center and/or the child’s food 
47:1439:109465:28:27:71:492:593:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:consumption, weight, and food security; they included: child gender and race-ethnicity 
47:1440:109552:27:28:71:538:566:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(Hispanic, Non-Hispanic black, or Non-Hispanic other versus Non-Hispanic white), whether the 
47:1441:109645:28:27:71:529:538:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:home language is not English or the mother was born outside of the U.S., whether the family’s 
47:1442:109739:27:28:71:537:511:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:income is below 100% of the federal poverty line (versus 100 to 185% of poverty), the mother’s 
47:1443:109834:28:28:71:539:483:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:education level (less than high school or high school graduate versus more than high school), the 
47:1444:109932:28:27:71:522:455:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:mother’s employment status (full-time or part-time versus not employed), whether the family 
47:1445:110024:27:28:71:530:428:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:had rules about food the child could eat, whether the mother reported that a small group size in 
47:1446:110121:28:27:71:541:400:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:child care was important to her child care selection, whether she had difficulty finding child care, 
47:1447:110222:27:28:71:522:373:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:whether she was married, her age (less than 25, 25 to 29, 35 to 39, or 40 or more versus 30 to 
47:1448:110317:28:28:71:520:345:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:34), whether the family had received WIC (for the study child) or Food Stamps since the last 
47:1449:110410:28:27:71:537:317:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:interview, whether the child was born low birth weight, whether the child was lactose intolerant, 
47:1450:110508:27:28:71:539:290:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the number of child’s well-child doctor visits since the last interview (zero or one, or two, versus 
47:1451:110609:28:27:71:536:262:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:three or more), whether the child was ever breast fed, whether the mother’s health was excellent 
47:1452:110706:27:28:71:539:235:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:or very good, whether the child was in multiple care arrangements, whether the child spent 30 or 
47:1453:110803:28:28:71:535:207:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:more hours in care, and the percentage of residents of the family’s ZIP code who were Hispanic 
47:1454:110898:28:27:71:496:179:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and non-Hispanic black.  We also adjust in regression models, but do not show: dummy 
47:1455:110983:27:28:71:536:152:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:variables for the child’s age (in months) at the four year follow up interview, whether the parent 
47:1456:111082:28:27:71:527:124:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:respondent was the child’s mother, the parent’s sampling weight from the four year follow up, 
47:1457:111176:27:0:71:522:97:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and dummy indicators of the state or region where the child lived. Ten states with 25 or more 
48:1458:111318:0:28:72:501:704:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:study children had their own dummy variable; other states were indicated by their region 
48:1459:111407:28:27:71:244:676:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(Northeast, Midwest, West, South). 
48:1460:111442:27:28:107:527:649:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:A:Center covariates.— Our regression analyses are restricted to four-year-old children in 
48:1461:111530:28:28:71:508:621:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:center care.  We include in these models characteristics of centers that may influence their 
48:1462:111623:28:27:71:511:593:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:CACFP participation decision and affect outcomes of children in their care. These controls 
48:1463:111714:27:28:71:476:566:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:include the center’s location (community-based center, preschool, school-based pre-
48:1464:111797:28:27:71:536:538:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:kindergarten, or something else), accreditation status, employee turnover rate, and the director’s 
48:1465:111896:27:28:71:513:511:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:years of experience at the center.  Although the survey information is not precise enough to 
48:1466:111988:28:28:71:529:483:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:determine eligibility among for-profit centers, we do know whether the center accepts children 
48:1467:112083:28:27:71:513:455:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:from or refers children to Head Start, and whether the center reports a willingness to accept 
48:1468:112177:27:28:72:529:428:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:subsidies.  To approximate total benefit levels, we use license status and licensed capacity (not 
48:1469:112275:28:27:72:468:400:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:licensed versus licensed for 50 or fewer, 51 to 100, or more than 100 children).11   
48:1470:112360:27:28:108:501:373:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:A:Child nutritional outcomes.— At the four year follow-up, the mother reported the 
48:1471:112441:28:28:72:537:345:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:frequency with which the child drank milk, juice, and soda and consumed fruits, vegetables, fast 
48:1472:112538:28:27:72:515:317:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:food, sweet snacks, and salty snacks over the seven days prior to the interview.  We created 
48:1473:112631:27:28:72:531:290:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:dummy variables to distinguish between children who drank two or more cups of drinks or had 
48:1474:112723:28:27:72:531:262:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:two or more servings per day of foods, versus those who consumed less.  We used the cutoff of 
48:1475:112817:27:28:72:523:235:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:two based roughly on the CACFP meal guidelines and other nutritional guidelines (American 
48:1476:112907:28:28:72:524:207:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Heart Association n.d.).  The mother was explicitly instructed to think about all the meals and 
48:1477:113003:28:27:72:522:179:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:snacks the child had from the time she got up until the time she went to bed.  She was further 
48:1478:113098:27:8:72:219:152:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:                                                 
48:1479:113146:8:18:72:520:144:49:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:11 We define the variable in this way because unlicensed centers were not asked their size in the main 
48:1480:113249:18:12:71:539:126:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:interview.  A subset of directors who were selected for their center to be observed reported the center size 
48:1481:113358:12:13:71:527:114:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:on a self-administered questionnaire.  Based on this report, although a similar proportion of unlicensed 
48:1482:113463:13:13:71:516:101:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:and licensed centers were large in size (had more than 100 children, 43 percent of unlicensed and 40 
48:1483:113564:13:12:71:510:88:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:percent of licensed) a higher percentage of unlicensed centers were small (less than 50 children, 37 
48:1484:113665:12:0:71:477:76:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:F:percent versus 28 percent) than mid-size (51 to 100 children, 20 percent versus 32 percent). 
49:1485:113806:0:28:72:512:704:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:asked to “Be sure to include food {CHILD} ate at home, preschool, restaurants, play dates, 
49:1486:113897:28:27:72:535:676:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:anywhere else, and over the weekend.” For juice, mothers were told to include 100% fruit juice, 
49:1487:113993:27:28:72:539:649:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and to not include “punch, Sunny Delight, Kool-Aid, sport drinks or other fruit-flavored drinks.” 
49:1488:114091:28:28:72:523:621:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Instead, mothers were asked to include these fruit-flavored drinks with their reports about the 
49:1489:114187:28:27:72:518:593:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:child drinking soda.  For vegetables, the mother was asked to exclude French fries and other 
49:1490:114280:27:28:72:489:566:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:fried potatoes, but to “include vegetables like those served in a stir-fry, soup, or stew.” 
49:1491:114372:28:27:108:540:538:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Children’s height and weight were measured by interviewers with a stadiometer ruler and 
49:1492:114460:27:28:72:540:511:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:digital bathroom scale. Two measurements were taken for both the child’s height and weight and 
49:1493:114555:28:28:72:510:483:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the measurements were averaged. Based on measured height and weight, we computed the 
49:1494:114640:28:27:72:493:455:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:child’s body mass index (BMI) then defined the child as underweight (less than the 5th 
49:1495:114727:27:28:72:533:428:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percentile), healthy weight (5th percentile to less than the 85th percentile), at risk of overweight 
49:1496:114827:28:27:72:535:400:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(85th to less than the 95th percentile) and overweight (equal to or great than the 95th percentile) 
49:1497:114927:27:28:72:375:373:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:based on CDC Growth Charts appropriate for the child’s age.   
49:1498:114989:28:28:108:533:345:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Parents reported food insecurity for the family as a whole and specific to the child using 
49:1499:115080:28:27:72:529:317:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the 18 item Current Population Survey-Food Security Scale (CPS-FSS; Nord et al. 2009).  The 
49:1500:115172:27:28:72:498:290:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:standard continuously scored measure was highly skewed because few sample members 
49:1501:115254:28:27:72:530:262:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:endorsed the items.  Thus, we created a dichotomous indicator of whether the mother endorsed 
49:1502:115347:27:28:72:523:235:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:any item about the children in the household (of eight items such as whether children’s meals 
49:1503:115441:28:28:72:536:207:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:were reduced in size, children skipped a meal or went hungry, or did not eat a balanced meal) or 
49:1504:115538:28:27:72:521:179:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the entire household (which was based on the eight child items as well as 10 additional items 
49:1505:115632:27:28:72:503:152:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:such as whether the adults cut the size of meals or skipped meals and whether the mother 
49:1506:115721:28:27:72:523:124:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:currently worried food would run out or the household couldn't afford to eat balanced meals). 
49:1507:115815:27:0:108:540:97:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:We also include lagged child outcomes from the two year follow up in some models.  We 
50:1508:115949:0:28:72:535:704:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:dummy coded whether the mother reported that the two-year-old child drank milk at both meals 
50:1509:116042:28:27:72:542:676:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and snacks, meals only, snacks only, or neither.  We used the child’s measured height and weight 
50:1510:116139:27:28:72:533:649:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:to calculate the child’s Body Mass Index (BMI) at age two.12  We also include lagged measures 
50:1511:116233:28:27:72:518:621:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of household and child food insecurity when the child was two-years-old, based on the same 
50:1512:116324:27:28:72:497:594:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:scale as used at the four year follow up, with two dummies: any food insecurity for both 
50:1513:116413:28:28:72:510:566:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:household and child and any food insecurity for the household but not the child, versus the 
50:1514:116505:28:27:71:273:538:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f6:B:reference category of no food insecurity.  
50:1515:116547:27:8:71:219:511:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:                                                 
50:1516:116595:8:16:72:525:503:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:12 Due to missing data on two year old BMI, we included a dummy indicator of not missing two year old BMI in 
50:1517:116704:16:0:71:368:487:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:regression models and assigned missing two year old BMI values to zero.
